everything in the channel + 1 for\n\t\t// the batch being processed.\n\t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n\t}\n}\n\n// Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n// cannot be added and must be retried.\nfunc (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n\tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n\tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n\t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n\t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n\t// in the batch size calculation.\n\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n\tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n\tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n\t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. This creates a race condition where enqueue holds a reference to the old queues array while reshardLoop is replacing it entirely. The real problem is that enqueue calculates the shard index using the current queue count, but that count can change mid-operation. If enqueue reads len(s.queues) = 4 and calculates shard = ref % 4, then tries to access s.queues[shard] while reshardLoop is simultaneously rebuilding the queues array with 6 shards, the index becomes invalid. The RLock in enqueue should prevent stop() from acquiring a WLock, but the issue is more fundamental—the shard calculation and the queue access aren't atomic with respect to resharding. The reshardLoop stops old shards, then starts new ones (line 1193-1194). The comment indicates this ordering ensures samples are delivered in order since old shards are completely flushed before new ones begin. However, there's a critical issue: start() resets pendingSamples to 0 (line 1241), but in-flight samples from the old shards may still be processing. During resharding, old queues are replaced with new ones that have different shard counts, but samples already enqueued in the old queues may not transfer properly to the new configuration. The enqueue logic needs examination to understand how samples are routed when the shard count changes.\n\nLooking at the enqueue function, I see a critical race condition: `len(s.queues)` is used to calculate which shard receives a sample, but this value changes during resharding. If a sample's shard index is calculated based on the old queue count (say, 4 shards) but then the queues are replaced with a new count (6 shards), the sample gets enqueued to the wrong destination. The reshardLoop acquires a write lock when starting new shards, but there's a window where the queue length changes mid-calculation. stop() will eventually release RLock and acquire WLock. Once enqueue finishes and releases its RLock, stop() can proceed to take WLock. The key insight is that RLock and WLock have different blocking semantics: multiple readers can hold RLock simultaneously, but a writer taking WLock will block all readers. So when stop() tries to acquire WLock after closing softShutdown, it will block any new enqueue calls that attempt to acquire RLock, but existing readers won't be forced to release their locks immediately. Lock() blocks all readers. So the sequence is: enqueue holds RLock, stop() acquires RLock (they coexist), then stop() releases it and acquires Lock() which waits for enqueue to finish. Once enqueue releases RLock, stop() can proceed with the write lock.\n\nThe real issue emerges with the queues themselves. When stop() releases the write lock, the queues array still references the old queues. Then start() creates new ones and reassigns the array. If enqueue() runs during this window—after reading the old queue count but before start() completes—there's a mismatch between what enqueue cached and what actually exists.\n\nBut reshardLoop runs synchronously: stop() blocks completely before start() is invoked. This means enqueue calls either finish before stop() acquires the write lock, or they see softShutdown already closed and return false. By the time start() runs and replaces the queues, no concurrent enqueue operations are active. The softShutdown channel acts as the synchronization point, preventing new enqueues from proceeding once resharding begins.\n\nHowever, the issue mentions \"shards stall\" after resharding, which suggests something's still going wrong. If a hard shutdown occurred and some samples were dropped, pendingSamples was correctly decremented via Sub(). But then Set(0) forces it to zero regardless, masking whether samples were actually lost or properly accounted for. This becomes problematic when samples remain in flight or when the shutdown wasn't clean.\n\nLooking deeper at the stop() flow, there's another concern: when the flush deadline times out at line 1289, the code doesn't exit early. Instead it proceeds directly to hardShutdown() and then waits on s.done again, meaning the timeout doesn't actually terminate the wait—it just triggers a forced shutdown while still blocking until completion.\n\nSince hardShutdown() cancels the context and causes all runShard goroutines to exit (closing s.done), stop() will always wait for shards to finish their cleanup and metric updates before returning. This means the Set(0) call in start() should be safe because it only executes after all previous operations have completed.\n\nThe reshardLoop also enforces this ordering—it calls stop() synchronously before start(), so there's no window where a shard could be updating metrics while start() resets them.\n\nHowever, if a shard goroutine somehow hangs and never decrements s.running, then s.done would never close and stop() would block indefinitely. The defer block that closes s.done only triggers when s.running reaches 0, so any stuck goroutine would prevent this from happening.\n\nThe hardShutdown() call after the timeout attempts to force exit by canceling the context, which should cause runShard to unblock from ctx.Done(). But if a goroutine is blocked on something else—like waiting on batchQueue or the timer—it might not respond to the context cancellation. When runShard tries to receive from the closed batchQueue, it gets ok=false and returns (line 1581-1582)\n\nSo this mechanism should ensure that all runShard goroutines exit when stop() is called.\n\nBut wait! There's an issue! Look at line 1448-1450:\n```go\nfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n    time.Sleep(time.Second)}\n```\n\nThe loop checks if there's a partial batch and tries to enqueue it. It sleeps 1 second and retries. But this loop will run FOREVER if the batchQueue channel is always full!The done channel passed to tryEnqueueingBatch is s.done from the shards, which is only closed when s.running reaches 0.\n\nSo if the batchQueue is full and we can't enqueue the partial batch, tryEnqueueingBatch returns true, and the loop retries. But if no one is reading from the batchQueue (because runShard exited), the queue will never drain, and the loop will retry forever!\n\nBut wait, looking at tryEnqueueingBatch (line 1459-1477):\n```go\nfunc (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n    q.batchMtx.Lock()\n    defer q.batchMtx.Unlock()    if len(q.batch) == 0 {\n        return false\n    }        select {\n    case q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n        return false    case <-done:\n        // The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n        // No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n        return false    default:\n        // The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n        return true\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAh! There's a check for done at line 1469. If the shard has been hard shut down (s.done is closed), tryEnqueueingBatch returns false and exits the loop! So the flow is: stop() calls FlushAndShutdown, which tries to enqueue remaining batches but exits early if the shard's done channel closes. This prevents the infinite retry loop—once the shard shuts down, the function stops trying to enqueue and proceeds to close the batchQueue.\n\nThe real concern is timing: if the batchQueue fills up while FlushAndShutdown is still running, it'll retry with a 1-second sleep. But if runShard isn't draining the queue fast enough, those buffered batches could be lost when the queue closes.\n\nLooking at the actual failure mode—samples stuck pending with no progress after resharding—this suggests the new runShard goroutines might not be reading from their queues at all. A panic or deadlock in the new shards would cause this. Or perhaps during resharding, samples get dropped in the hard shutdown, but the pending metrics don't get reset, creating the illusion of stuck data.\n\nBut there's another possibility: what if pendingSamples.Set(0) races with incoming enqueue() calls? If stop() completes and start() resets the counter to zero while scraping goroutines are simultaneously enqueueing samples to the fresh queues, the pending count could become inconsistent with actual queue contents. The system would think everything's flushed when samples are actually accumulating. enqueue() calls return false. So no new samples are enqueued during the resharding window.\n\nWhen start() recreates softShutdown (line 1253), there's a brief period where the old channel is closed but the new one hasn't been created yet. This means enqueue() fails temporarily, then succeeds again once start() completes. The Set(0) call happens after locking, ensuring pendingSamples is reset before the new softShutdown channel opens for business.\n\nAny enqueue() attempt during this transition either hits the closed channel and fails, or arrives after start() has already set up the new queues and succeeds. The real concern is what happens if scraping continues trying to push samples while resharding is in progress—samples get dropped until the new queues are ready.\n\nBut there's a timing issue I'm noticing: numShards gets updated immediately at lines 1073-1074, before the actual resharding work begins. The reshardChan is sent asynchronously, so there's a window where numShards reflects the desired state but the queues haven't been recreated yet. This could create a mismatch between what the system thinks is happening and what's actually Either the goroutines fail to start, get blocked during initialization, or exit prematurely before draining any work.\n\nLooking at the newQueue initialization, I notice the batchQueue channel is created with a specific buffer capacity calculated from the ratio of total capacity to batch size. If batches calculates to zero, it defaults to 1. This means the channel might have very limited buffering, potentially causing the queue to fill up and block producers before consumers even begin processing.\n\nThe resharding scenario is worth considering too—when shards rebalance from 4 to 6, some shards will receive more samples than before. If a shard suddenly handles increased load but its runShard goroutine can't keep pace, samples could accumulate faster than they're being sent, causing backpressure throughout the pipeline. This isn't necessarily a bug, but rather a capacity constraint that becomes apparent under the new shard distribution.\n\nLooking more carefully at the code, the most suspicious part is the Set(0) call during start(). When old shards shut down, there's a window where samples have been sent to the remote endpoint but their metrics haven't been decremented yet—they're still in-flight. If a hard shutdown occurs during this window, those in-flight samples never get their Sub() call, and then Set(0) wipes the counter clean, losing track of them entirely. Though examining the hard shutdown logic at lines 1563-1578, it does appear to record all dropped samples including in-flight ones, so this should theoretically be handled correctly. The actual issue might be something else entirely.\n\nThe Set(0) at line 1241 could be masking a deeper problem—if the hard shutdown logic has a bug where certain samples aren't being accounted for in the dropped count, the unconditional reset would hide that failure. I need to look for places where samples are processed but might not have corresponding Sub() calls to decrement the pending Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe intermittent stalling of remote-write shards correlates with a metric inconsistency during resharding: the `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` counter is unconditionally reset to 0 during new shard initialization (line 1241 in `queue_manager.go`), potentially hiding samples that were dropped during hard shutdown or lost in partial batches.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n\n**Critical Issue:** In the `(*shards).start()` function at line 1241:\n```go\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n```\n\nThis operation unconditionally resets the global pending samples counter to 0 **without accounting for samples that may have been lost during the hard shutdown phase** of the preceding resharding cycle.\n\n**Mechanism:**\n\n1. **Resharding Sequence** (lines 1193-1194):\n   - `reshardLoop()` calls `t.shards.stop()` to gracefully shut down old shards\n   - Then calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` to initialize new shards with new queue count\n\n2. **Hard Shutdown Occurs If Flushing Times Out** (lines 1289-1294):\n   - `stop()` waits for old queues to flush within `flushDeadline`\n   - If timeout: `s.hardShutdown()` cancels the context\n   - Running shards exit early without completing pending RPCs\n   - Dropped samples are recorded via `pendingSamples.Sub()` (line 1569)\n\n3. **Counter Reset Overwrites Metrics** (line 1241):\n   - After `stop()` returns, `start()` is immediately called\n   - `pendingSamples.Set(0)` unconditionally sets the counter to 0\n   - **This overwrites any Sub() operations recorded during hard shutdown**\n   - The Prometheus Gauge's `Set()` replaces the value, not adding to it\n\n4. **Partial Batch Loss Scenario**:\n   - Samples in a queue's partial batch may not be sent to batchQueue before hard shutdown\n   - `FlushAndShutdown()` (line 1447-1455) tries to enqueue the batch\n   - If hard shutdown happens before enqueue succeeds, the partial batch is abandoned (line 1453: `q.batch = nil`)\n   - These samples were already counted in `pendingSamples` via `enqueue()`\n   - But they're never sent or properly accounted for in dropped metrics\n   - Then `start()` resets `pendingSamples.Set(0)`, hiding the loss\n\n## Evidence\n\n**File:** `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n\n### Key Code References:\n\n1. **Problematic Reset** (line 1241):\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n       s.mtx.Lock()\n       defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // ← ISSUE: Unconditional reset\n   ```\n\n2. **Hard Shutdown Mechanism** (lines 1289-1294):\n   ```go\n   select {\n   case <-s.done:\n       return\n   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):  // ← Timeout triggers hard shutdown\n   }\n   s.hardShutdown()  // ← Cancels context, causes runShard to exit early\n   <-s.done\n   ```\n\n3. **Metrics Update During Hard Shutdown** (lines 1563-1578):\n   ```go\n   case <-ctx.Done():\n       droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // ← Sub() call\n       // ... record failures ...\n       return  // ← Exit immediately\n   ```\n\n4. **Flush and Shutdown with Potential Loss** (lines 1447-1455):\n   ```go\n   func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n       for q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {  // ← Retry loop\n           time.Sleep(time.Second)\n       }\n       q.batchMtx.Lock()\n       defer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n       q.batch = nil  // ← Samples lost if not yet enqueued\n       close(q.batchQueue)\n   ```\n\n5. **tryEnqueueingBatch Exit on Hard Shutdown** (lines 1459-1477):\n   ```go\n   case <-done:\n       // The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n       // No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n       return false  // ← Exits loop, abandoning partial batch\n   ```\n\n### Related Tests:\n\n- `TestReshardPartialBatch()` (queue_manager_test.go): Tests for deadlocks during resharding with partial batches\n- `TestReshardRaceWithStop()`: Tests race conditions between resharding and shutdown\n- `TestReshard()`: Basic resharding functionality test\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**:\n   - `(*QueueManager).updateShardsLoop()` (line 1057): Triggers resharding\n   - `(*QueueManager).reshardLoop()` (line 1184): Executes resharding sequence\n   - `(*shards).start()` (line 1237): Initializes new shards\n   - `(*shards).stop()` (line 1269): Gracefully shuts down old shards\n   - `(*shards).enqueue()` (line 1312): Routes samples to shards\n   - `(*queue).FlushAndShutdown()` (line 1447): Flushes queue during shutdown\n\n2. **Metrics Package** (`prometheus/prometheus/model/metrics`):\n   - `prometheus.Gauge.Set()`: Overwrites counter value (not additive)\n   - `prometheus.Gauge.Sub()`: Decrements counter value\n\n3. **Sync Primitives**:\n   - `sync.RWMutex` on `shards.mtx`: Protects queues access\n   - `sync.Atomic` counters: Track pending samples per shard\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Option 1 (Recommended): Remove the `Set(0)` call**\n- The counter should already be 0 if all old samples are properly accounted for\n- Rationale: By the time `start()` is called, all old shards have finished\n  - Either normally: all samples sent via `updateMetrics().Sub()`\n  - Or via hard shutdown: all samples dropped via `Sub()` at line 1569\n- Remove line 1241: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)`\n\n**Option 2: Use `Sub()` to explicitly account for remaining pending samples**\n```go\n// Before creating new queues, subtract remaining pending samples\nremaining := s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Desc()  // Or track separately\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(remaining)\n```\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Monitor Resharding Events**:\n   - Enable debug logging for \"Remote storage resharding\" messages\n   - Correlate with timestamp of metric stalls\n\n2. **Check Metric Anomalies**:\n   - Watch for `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` jumping to 0\n   - Compare with `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_total` and `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_total{exported}`\n   - If pending suddenly drops to 0 while total is increasing, resharding occurred\n\n3. **Add Instrumentation**:\n   - Log the value of `pendingSamples` before/after `Set(0)` call\n   - Log samples dropped during hard shutdown\n   - Compare the two to detect loss\n\n4. **Monitor These Metrics During Resharding**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`: Should be 0 after flush completes\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total`: Should increase if hard shutdown occurs\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shard_capacity`: Capacity of each shard\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards`: Number of active shards\n\n5. **Reproduce Scenario**:\n   ```bash\n   # Monitor metrics during target scrape changes\n   # Observe when \"Remote storage resharding\" log appears\n   # Check if pending samples becomes inconsistent\n   # Verify samples reach remote destination\n   ```\n\n## Timeline of Events Leading to Stall\n\n1. **T0**: Target discovery changes → New scrape targets added/removed\n2. **T1**: Data rate changes → updateShardsLoop detects need to reshard (4→6 shards)\n3. **T2**: updateShardsLoop sends to reshardChan, sets `t.numShards = 6`\n4. **T3**: reshardLoop receives and calls `stop()`:\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel\n   - Calls `FlushAndShutdown()` for each old queue\n5. **T4**: If flush takes >flushDeadline:\n   - Hard shutdown triggered\n   - Old runShard goroutines exit early (line 1578)\n   - Partial batches in queues are abandoned\n   - `pendingSamples.Sub()` records some dropped samples\n6. **T5**: `start()` called with new queues:\n   - **BUG**: `pendingSamples.Set(0)` resets counter\n   - New runShard goroutines started\n7. **T6**: New samples enqueued to new shards\n   - Metric shows pending samples increasing\n   - But previously dropped samples are not reflected\n8. **T7**: If remote storage is missing old samples:\n   - Gaps in data\n   - Possible data inconsistency in remote system\n\n## Why This Is Intermittent\n\n- **Race Condition Dependent**: Only manifests when hard shutdown timeout occurs\n- **Load Dependent**: More likely under high cardinality (many series) or slow remote endpoint\n- **Timing Dependent**: Depends on exact timing of resharding vs batch flush\n- **Network Dependent**: Slow or unresponsive remote endpoint triggers timeout\n- **Target Discovery Pattern**: Specific patterns of target changes trigger threshold-crossing resharding\n\n## Confirmation
